<review>Cool little spot Dark Heart had live music, a food truck, cornhole and a giant connect four. The band was out front so next time I would bring my own chairs just incase (since that seemed liked the pace to be). They also have a back patio, indoor seating and dog area. It was fun to people watch and see everyone enjoying their time laughing and dancing. The food tuck onsite was Ash and Oil. It was pretty delicious. The beers on tap hit the spot. Just a heads up place is tucked away so look for the signage. <rating>5</rating><review>For being a new brewery these guys certainly have a large variety of beers to pick from. Quite a few IPA options as well as some unique options like a Scottish ale and cream ale. The hazy IPA was solid, but definitely give the Captain Krohn a try, it was delicious! The location isn't the greatest as you can't see it from the street, just look for the sign and go through the gate. It shares a parking lot with a bunch of junk cars unfortunately, so parking may be tight. Once you get inside though the space is nice and cozy with multiple TVs and a convenient popcorn machine. Service is friendly and helpful as well!<//review><pics>[{'url': ['https://lh5.googleusercontent.com/p/AF1QipPpoxufI0ku-a4PIY6mGHKs4_4YLYgLJm3tttn3=w150-h150-k-no-p']}, {'url': ['https://lh5.googleusercontent.com/p/AF1QipOIUPkZ8o5GuFzVyOM2IwA-W2FkG_BSC10f1aBk=w150-h150-k-no-p']}, {'url': ['https://lh5.googleusercontent.com/p/AF1QipNvloF9ZMS8r_d6t7wzZ69tI2oktrryBPdshQNa=w150-h150-k-no-p']}]<//pics>< resp>

< text>
So my daughter's wanted to take me on a pre Father's day out they wanted to take me to a brewery. I did some research and chose this place due to the raving Yelp reviews. I stepped out to make sure they had dine in due to the pandemic. I noticed a woman with a t-shirt on with their logo, it was safe to assume she worked there. I stepped inside, she was holding a conversation with a couple, as I was standing in plain view, I waited for a break in the conversation. I had to say excuse me twice before she acknowledged me. We went in, went to the counter and the gentleman was very nice and patient as we chose our samplers. Their website said they have food, not true. $5.00 lunchables. There was a Filipino food truck outside that didn't have what we wanted on the menu.  She brought over our order and I tried to talk with her, but she seemed to be in a hurry to get away. There were only 6 people in the establishment. The service from her was not good. With that being said, service is important to me. I will not go there again.< /text>

< Text>
This place is fantastic!  I'm from WA State where it seems that we have a microbrewery on every corner, and I'm going to say that this is one of my favorites!  They have 3 (I think) options for flights.  I got the 6-sample flight, and I hated none of what I sampled.  The hazy IPA, oatmeal stout, and peanut butter stout were my favorites.  They even offer complimentary vegetable soup!   I don't know if they always have time to do this, but they even came around at one point and offered to refill my water and soup bowl.  I highly recommend this place and might even ask if I can take a growler or two home to Washington.<//Text>

<Text>Our family cat had been suffering w/ hyperthyroid and kidney failure for some time.  We had opted out of treating because he was semi-feral and did not take to us sticking tubes down his throat every day.  Instead, we tried to make his life as easy as possible and when he got picky with his food, my mom fed him people food.  However, after a couple of years of this, we got the feeling the end was near as food (even people food) become unappetizing.  We had heard of services which would come to you so you could say goodbye to your pet at home where he/she is most comfortable.  One of the volunteers at Kitten Rescue recommended Choice Veterinary Care.  We had called another place recommended by another vet but Choice seemed to be more informed and knowledgeable.

We are incredibly grateful for the vets at Choice.  We spoke to Dr. Amy at first to discuss our situation and she made us feel comfortable with our choice.  Because the team at Choice are all vets, they all know about the various illnesses afflicting the cats and were very helpful explaining our cat's behavior.  We have known for a while that our cat was not going to get better and we wanted to make sure he had gotten the most quality life possible w/ the least amount of suffering.

Dr. Peter was assigned to us and he was incredible patient...he explained again how our cat's illness had progressed and made us feel comfortable with our situation.  He explained the whole process of how the euthanasia would work.  When the time came to say goodbye, he was so gentle with our cat.  A week after the euthanasia, a member of the Choice Team dropped off our cat's ashes in person.

There is really no easy way to say goodbye to a loved family member but we felt so supported by Choice.  Our goal was to have our family cat suffer the least amount possible and taking him to a vet would have been too cruel and stressful for him. <Review>I‚Äôve visited Nicholson Ranch twice (once in 2011 and once in 2019) and had a great experience both times. Friendly staff and delicious Old World style wines.  We showed up just as they were closing this time, unfortunately, but they were kind enough to give us a free pour of their 2013 Pinot Noir and let us wander around the grounds.  Thanks!

1h 10min from SoMa (45 mi)
No Reservations Needed
Open Daily, 10am-6pm

$20 / person tasting for 4 Estate wines in Tasting Room
$40 / person tasting for 6 Estate and Reserve wins in the Courtyard
$40 / person cave tour and 6 tastings (Reservation Required)
$30 / person Lakeside tasting of four Estate wines with vineyard tour (Reso req‚Äôd)

Pros:
* Convenient location right off Highway 12
* Open later than most wineries (closes at 6pm)
* The wines are very good, Old World-style wines, particularly Pinot Noir and Chardonnay
* Very friendly and knowledgeable servers
* Beautiful views of the surrounding Carneros region
* Picnic tables and a nice lake, perfect for packing a lunch and buying a bottle
* Nice hike up to a chapel on a hill
* Many tasting and tour options, including a cave tour

Cons:
* Prices have more than doubled since my last visit
* The surrounding area was sadly damaged during the 2018 wildfires
* Tasting room is a bit lackluster, but outside is nice
* Convenient location also means views of the roadways</Review>< user_id>

I loved the little greek chapel on the hill and beautiful little pond area for tastings. The patio and personal service was fantastic for our small group, they host large groups both inside and outside as well. The winery survived last year's fires, but the main house had been lost to the fire as was a portion of their vines. <user_name>Brent Riffel< /user_name><time>1476641991789< /time><rate>1</rate>< text>
I will avoid this winery in the future. I am Bay Area resident  and go wine tasting a couple times a year for special occasions. Usually you pay a nominal fee $10 - 20 for a tasting of 5+ wines and there are a few bottles not on the list that are open and the winery would like to share. The staff or wine maker are  excited to tell you about the character of the wine based on where it was grown,  the weather that year, etc.  Tasting fees are often waived with purchase of a bottle --- NOT at this place!

This place felt like a tourist trap. The tasting was $30 for six wines. My wife and I shared one and decided we'd get a bottle if we liked what we tried and see of they would waive the fee. The server was not knowledgable about the wines and smarmy. He seemed to bragging about his scholastic achievement (it was not that impressive). He actually looked at my wife and said "can I teach you something young lady" and told her that she shouldn't drink water between tastings.  She had asked for a oyster cracker or something to clear her pallet and they had none - water was the next best thing. We were trying to decide between the two Pinot Noirs on the list. The server had mixed them up at one point and we were trying to decide which bottle to take.  She was annoyed.

We bought the bottle of the Sonoma Coast Pinot Noir the fee was not waived. I was hoping for a nice romantic treat after visiting an old family  friend in Sonoma, instead I left feeling insulted and hustled.< /text>

<rate>3< /rate><review>Place is hip and relatively clean. They have individual chairs that added to the decor, but I miss my massage chairs. Their pillow was a bit itchy, but then again I was wearing a linen shirt. I would call it a simple up to-do -date nail salon.

There were only four workers today around the late afternoon on a Monday, not including the receptionist. So as I sat down, I was offered tea, coffee, or water. Nice! Waited for 45 mins before they started on me, not so nice! I really hate places that makes you wait so long especially when you made an appointment. I like to keep my schedule :)

Besides that downfall, the workers there all seem to be working hard as a team. 3/4 workers had done some work on me, which is sort of annoying when it comes to tipping. I want to give it a good tip, but when it's all scattered, the tips are going to be divided among them. Oh well!

They soak your feet in individual bags, which seems cleaner than the regular massage chair tub. I would imagine they change the bag every other customers or so. At least, I hope so!

So who's good or who's not? I didn't get their names, yikes! There were three females and one male. The male didn't work on me. They were all very good with massage and paint. I hate it when they don't clean up the edges or uneven polish, no complaints from me at this salon with those. I would just suggest if you like harder pressure on your massages, let em' know!

Before I end my entry, I want to note that their polish all seems new and in good quality (mostly OPI and Essie). I hate places that keep old nail polish in stock...anyways, hope this helps!</review><Pics>None<//Pics><response>None< /response><GmapID>0x80c2ba66d035b1af:0xbc85ae7310241f22<//GmapID></record></dataset><record>

<UserId.>115525113560206764538</UserId.><username>Kevin Kou<//username><time>1600378440193< /time><rate>5<//rate><Text>As a non-Korean, I've been coming here for 9 years and it's consistently gone unnoticed because it specializes a few soupy dishes that aren't what most people go for when they think "Korean". It's pretty simple: you choose 1 of 3 soups (chicken, hangover, or goat soup)

- Chicken ginseng: a whole small chicken stuffed with rice, root vegetables, dates and herbs; super clean and excellent for someone feeling under the weather.
- Hangover: for the more-adventurous types because it has some chunks of meat, oxblood and tripe in it; great for hangovers
- Goat: my personal favorite, a perfect balance of herbs, spices, vegetables, and gamey meat; great for all occasions but especially winter

I'm happy to see that it's still doing well under covid circumstances and felt safe going the other day when they converted most of the parking lot into an outdoor, socially-distanced, and tented dining setup. Parking might be a bit tough since the restaurant next door (Parks BBQ) always draws a crowd.

You probably won't be able to finish the whole serving of soup since you're also eating rice and delicious banchan (free side dishes), which is awesome since they usually refill your soup when you ask for a takeout box. Despite coming for so many years, nobody ever remembers me, so it feels like everybody's extra nice to me (as an outsider?)

Whenever I leave LA I try to make this a priority on my return. The kind aunties who run the shop are still there, as are the crusty chainsmoking uncles. It feels normal, and that's nice.

Also, their hours might've changed a bit given covid. Not sure but they might be closed by 9?< /Text><pics>[{'url': ['https://lh5.googleusercontent.com/p/AF1QipOhYcmuG4SwXaK7rupjmLQFIcqVIWmOjB4SMFTD=w150-h150-k-no-p']}]</pics>< Resp>

<Rate>5< /Rate><Review>Jugos Vallarta has a wide variety of healthy meals as well as traditional Mexican plates some healthy some not so much. What really makes this place stand out is it's chocomiles (Mexican chocolate shakes) it's almost like the chocolate shakes you buy in Guadalajara Mex.
